In [2]:
#Q1 write a function in python to sum up a given set of numbers other than itself
input = [1,2,3,4]
output = []
for x in np.arange(len(input)):
    sum = 0
    for i in np.arange(len(input)):
        if(i!=x):
            sum += input[i]
    output.append(sum)
    
print(output)

#read csv file into pandas dataframe

#b. find the best performing product/highest sales product

highest_sales_product = sales.filter(regex=("W.*")).sum(axis=1).argmax()
print('Highest Sales Product: ' + highest_sales_product)

#validate if only one higest sales product
sales.filter(regex=("W.*")).sum(axis=1)[sales.filter(regex=("W.*")).sum(axis=1) == sales.filter(regex=("W.*")).sum(axis=1).max()]

In [6]:
#c. Most promising product (emerging product)
#rules: continuously grow in 52 weeks only take as consideration
for i in np.arange(len(sales_weekly)):
    sales = "increasing"
    #print("Product P",i)
    diff = sales_weekly.iloc[i].diff()
    for x in np.arange(0,51):
        if(diff[x+1]<diff[x]):
            sales="decreasing"
            #print(x, '.....',a[x+1],'....',a[x])
    if(sales == "increasing"):
        print("Product P",i, "is emerging")
        
#no emerging product

#d. worst performing product on biweekly basis

print("Worst Performing Product in a biweekly basis\n")
for x in np.arange(len(sales_weekly.columns))[::2]:
    y = x + 2
    print("Week" , x, "to Week", y)
    #print not only find min, but all minimum
    min_list = sales_weekly.iloc[:,x:y].sum(axis=1)[sales_weekly.iloc[:,x:y].sum(axis=1) == sales_weekly.iloc[:,x:y].sum(axis=1).min()].index
    print(', '.join(min_list))

In [8]:
#identify outlier from data by weeks number
for i in np.arange(len(sales_weekly)):
    mean = sales_weekly.iloc[i].mean()
    std = sales_weekly.iloc[i].std()
    list = []
    print("Product ", i+1)
    for x in np.arange(len(sales_weekly.columns)):
        if((sales_weekly.iloc[i][x] - mean) > std):
            string = "week" + str(x)
            list.append(string)
    print(','.join(list))

In [11]:
#read dataset into pandas dataframe

import dateutil.parser as dparser
import datetime
from pattern.en import singularize

jobpost = pd.read_csv("data job posts.csv")

jobpost['date'] = [dparser.parse(x) for x in jobpost['date']]
jobpost['date'] = [d.date() for d in jobpost.date]
jobpost['year'] = pd.DatetimeIndex(jobpost['date']).year
jobpost['month'] = pd.DatetimeIndex(jobpost['date']).month
In [12]:
#b. column extraction
jobpost_filtered = jobpost[['Title', 'Duration','Location','JobDescription', 'JobRequirment', 'RequiredQual','Salary','Deadline','AboutC']]
jobpost_filtered.rename(columns={'Title':'Job Title',
                        'Duration':'Position Duration',
                        'Location':'Position Location',
                        'JobDescription':'Job Description',
                        'JobRequirment':'Job Responsibilities',
                        'RequiredQual':'Required Qualifications',
                        'Salary':'Remuneration',
                        'Deadline':'Application Deadline',
                        'AboutC' : 'About Company'}, inplace=True)

In [22]:
#f and g
#store in new dataframe
newJobRequirement = pd.DataFrame(columns=['JobRequirement'])

#text mining
for x in np.arange(len(jobpost.JobRequirment)):
    print("Processing" , x+1)
    s=[]
    if(type(jobpost.JobRequirment[x]) == np.str): #Nan is float type, instead of check np.nan, compare str avoid code complex
        word_split = jobpost.JobRequirment[x].replace("stop","").split(" ")
        for i in word_split:
            s.append(singularize(i))
    s = ' '.join(s)
    newJobRequirement.loc[x] = s

#calculate similarity between description_x and description_y
def f(x):
    return fuzz.ratio(x[1],x[2])

#store in new column name resultant scores
testset['resultant_scores'] = testset.apply(f,axis=1)
In [26]:
#to prove the concept of parallelism is workable. 
import time
start_time = time.time()

newJobRequirement2 = pd.DataFrame(columns=['JobRequirement'])

def ratio(count,x,y):
    newJobRequirement2.loc[count]= fuzz.ratio(x,y)
    
for i in np.arange(len(testset)):
    ratio(i, testset.iloc[i][1],testset.iloc[i][2])
    
print("--- %s seconds ---" % (time.time() - start_time))

--- 1.542600393295288 seconds ---
In [27]:
import threading
from threading import Thread
import time

start_time = time.time()
newJobRequirement = pd.DataFrame(columns=['JobRequirement'])

def ratio(count,x,y):
    newJobRequirement.loc[count]= fuzz.ratio(x,y)
    
print("Start Multithreading Processing")
threads = []

for i in np.arange(len(testset)):
    t = threading.Thread(target=ratio, args=(i, testset.iloc[i][1],testset.iloc[i][2]))
    t.start()
    threads.append(t)
    
print("In the mean of processing...killing")

while len(threads) > 0:
    for index, thread in enumerate(threads):
        if(not thread.is_alive()):
            del threads[index]

print("Done, no alive threads")
print("--- %s seconds ---" % (time.time() - start_time))

Start Multithreading Processing
In the mean of processing...killing
Done, no alive threads
--- 1.4971868991851807 seconds ---
